	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" >Bill Gates</h1>
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		<div id="contentSub2"></div>
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the co-founder of Microsoft. For other people of the same name, see <a href="/wiki/Bill_Gates_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Bill Gates (disambiguation)">Bill Gates (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">American business magnate and philanthropist</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>

<p><b>William Henry Gates III</b>  (born October 28, 1955) is an American <a href="/wiki/Business_magnate" title="Business magnate">business magnate</a>, software developer, investor, author, and philanthropist. He is a co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManes199411_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManes199411-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:5_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> During his career at Microsoft, Gates held the positions of <a href="/wiki/Chairman" class="mw-redirect" title="Chairman">chairman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">chief executive officer</a> (CEO), <a href="/wiki/President_(corporate_title)" title="President (corporate title)">president</a> and <a href="/wiki/Software_architect" title="Software architect">chief software architect</a>, while also being the largest individual <a href="/wiki/Shareholder" title="Shareholder">shareholder</a> until May 2014. He is one of the best-known entrepreneurs and pioneers of the <a href="/wiki/Home_computer" title="Home computer">microcomputer revolution</a> of the 1970s and 1980s.
</p><p>Gates was born and raised in <a href="/wiki/Seattle,_Washington" class="mw-redirect" title="Seattle, Washington">Seattle, Washington</a>. In 1975, he co-founded Microsoft with childhood friend <a href="/wiki/Paul_Allen" title="Paul Allen">Paul Allen</a> in <a href="/wiki/Albuquerque,_New_Mexico" title="Albuquerque, New Mexico">Albuquerque, New Mexico</a>; it went on to become the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">personal computer</a> software company.<sup id="cite_ref-CNN_Tech_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_Tech-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> Gates led the company as chairman and CEO until stepping down as CEO in January 2000, but he remained chairman and became chief software architect.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> During the late 1990s, he had been <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Microsoft" title="Criticism of Microsoft">criticized for his business tactics</a>, which have been considered <a href="/wiki/Anti-competitive_practices" title="Anti-competitive practices">anti-competitive</a>. This opinion has been upheld by numerous court rulings.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELesinski200696Manes1994459_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELesinski200696Manes1994459-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> In June 2006, Gates announced that he would be transitioning to a part-time role at Microsoft and full-time work at the <a href="/wiki/Bill_%26_Melinda_Gates_Foundation" title="Bill &amp; Melinda Gates Foundation">Bill &amp; Melinda Gates Foundation</a>, the private charitable foundation that he and his wife, <a href="/wiki/Melinda_Gates" title="Melinda Gates">Melinda Gates</a>, established in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> He gradually transferred his duties to <a href="/wiki/Ray_Ozzie" title="Ray Ozzie">Ray Ozzie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Craig_Mundie" title="Craig Mundie">Craig Mundie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He stepped down as chairman of Microsoft in February 2014 and assumed a new post as technology adviser to support the newly appointed CEO <a href="/wiki/Satya_Nadella" title="Satya Nadella">Satya Nadella</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In March 2020, Gates left his board positions at Microsoft and <a href="/wiki/Berkshire_Hathaway" title="Berkshire Hathaway">Berkshire Hathaway</a> to focus on his philanthropic endeavors including <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, <a href="/wiki/Global_health" title="Global health">global health</a> and development, and education.<sup id="cite_ref-Haselton_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haselton-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 1987, he has been included in the <a href="/wiki/The_World%27s_Billionaires" title="The World&#39;s Billionaires"><i>Forbes</i> list of the world's wealthiest people</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Why_Isn&#39;t_on_&#39;Forbes&#39;_List_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Why_Isn&#39;t_on_&#39;Forbes&#39;_List-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FORBES_The_Next_Bill_Gates_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FORBES_The_Next_Bill_Gates-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> From 1995 to 2017, he held the <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> title of the richest person in the world all but four of those years.<sup id="cite_ref-Forbes_profile_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes_profile-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In October 2017, he was surpassed by <a href="/wiki/Amazon_(company)" title="Amazon (company)">Amazon</a> founder and CEO <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Bezos" title="Jeff Bezos">Jeff Bezos</a>, who had an estimated net worth of US$90.6&#160;billion compared to Gates's net worth of US$89.9&#160;billion at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-Forbes_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> As of January 2021, Gates had an estimated net worth of US$163&#160;billion, making him the third-richest person in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Later in his career and since leaving day-to-day operations at Microsoft in 2008, Gates has pursued a number of philanthropic endeavors. He has given sizable amounts of money to various charitable organizations and scientific research programs through the Bill &amp; Melinda Gates Foundation, reported to be the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Private_foundation" title="Private foundation">private charity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In 2009, Gates and <a href="/wiki/Warren_Buffett" title="Warren Buffett">Warren Buffett</a> founded <a href="/wiki/The_Giving_Pledge" title="The Giving Pledge">The Giving Pledge</a>, whereby they and other billionaires pledge to give at least half of their wealth to philanthropy.<sup id="cite_ref-Fortune_challenge_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortune_challenge-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#In_media"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">In media</span></a>

</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Gates was born in <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>, on October 28, 1955.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> He is the son of <a href="/wiki/William_H._Gates_Sr." class="mw-redirect" title="William H. Gates Sr.">William H. Gates Sr.</a><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> (1925–2020) and <a href="/wiki/Mary_Maxwell_Gates" title="Mary Maxwell Gates">Mary Maxwell Gates</a> (1929–1994).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> His ancestry includes English, German, and Irish/Scots-Irish.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> His father was a prominent lawyer, and his mother served on the board of directors for <a href="/wiki/First_Interstate_BancSystem" title="First Interstate BancSystem">First Interstate BancSystem</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Way_of_America" class="mw-redirect" title="United Way of America">United Way of America</a>. Gates's maternal grandfather was J. W. Maxwell, a national bank president. Gates has an older sister Kristi (Kristianne) and a younger sister Libby. He is the fourth of his name in his family but is known as William Gates III or "Trey" (i.e., three) because his father had the "II" suffix.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManes199415_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManes199415-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-leibovich20001231_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leibovich20001231-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The family lived in the <a href="/wiki/Sand_Point,_Seattle" title="Sand Point, Seattle">Sand Point</a> area of Seattle in a home that was damaged by a rare tornado when Gates was seven years old.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Early in his life, Gates observed that his parents wanted him to pursue a law career.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManes199447_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManes199447-27">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> When he was young, his family regularly attended a church of the <a href="/wiki/Congregational_Christian_Churches" title="Congregational Christian Churches">Congregational Christian Churches</a>, a Protestant Reformed denomination.<sup id="cite_ref-Congregational_1_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Congregational_1-28">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Congregational_2_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Congregational_2-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Congregational_3_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Congregational_3-30">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Gates was small for his age and was bullied as a child.<sup id="cite_ref-leibovich20001231_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leibovich20001231-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The family encouraged competition; one visitor reported that "it didn't matter whether it was <a href="/wiki/Hearts_(card_game)" title="Hearts (card game)">hearts</a> or <a href="/wiki/Pickleball" title="Pickleball">pickleball</a> or swimming to the dock; there was always a reward for winning and there was always a penalty for losing".<sup id="cite_ref-nerds2_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nerds2-31">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paul_Allen_and_Bill_Gates_at_Lakeside_School_in_1970.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Paul_Allen_and_Bill_Gates_at_Lakeside_School_in_1970.jpg/220px-Paul_Allen_and_Bill_Gates_at_Lakeside_School_in_1970.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Paul_Allen_and_Bill_Gates_at_Lakeside_School_in_1970.jpg/330px-Paul_Allen_and_Bill_Gates_at_Lakeside_School_in_1970.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Paul_Allen_and_Bill_Gates_at_Lakeside_School_in_1970.jpg/440px-Paul_Allen_and_Bill_Gates_at_Lakeside_School_in_1970.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="811" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paul_Allen_and_Bill_Gates_at_Lakeside_School_in_1970.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gates (right) with <a href="/wiki/Paul_Allen" title="Paul Allen">Paul Allen</a> at <a href="/wiki/Lakeside_School_(Seattle)" title="Lakeside School (Seattle)">Lakeside School</a> in 1970</div></div></div>
<p>At 13, he enrolled in the private <a href="/wiki/Lakeside_School_(Seattle,_Washington)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lakeside School (Seattle, Washington)">Lakeside prep school</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManes199424_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManes199424-32">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> where he wrote his first software program.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> When he was in the eighth grade, the Mothers' Club at the school used proceeds from Lakeside School's rummage sale to buy a <a href="/wiki/Teletype_Model_33" title="Teletype Model 33">Teletype Model 33</a> ASR terminal and a block of computer time on a <a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a> (GE) computer for the students.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManes199427_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManes199427-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Gates took an interest in programming the GE system in <a href="/wiki/BASIC_programming_language" class="mw-redirect" title="BASIC programming language">BASIC</a>, and he was excused from math classes to pursue his interest. He wrote his first computer program on this machine, an implementation of <a href="/wiki/Tic-tac-toe" title="Tic-tac-toe">tic-tac-toe</a> that allowed users to play games against the computer. Gates was fascinated by the machine and how it would always execute software code perfectly.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGates199612_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGates199612-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> After the Mothers Club donation was exhausted, Gates and other students sought time on systems including <a href="/wiki/Digital_Equipment_Corporation" title="Digital Equipment Corporation">DEC</a> <a href="/wiki/Programmed_Data_Processor" title="Programmed Data Processor">PDP</a> minicomputers. One of these systems was a <a href="/wiki/PDP-10" title="PDP-10">PDP-10</a> belonging to <a href="/wiki/Computer_Center_Corporation" title="Computer Center Corporation">Computer Center Corporation</a> (CCC) which banned for the summer Gates, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Allen" title="Paul Allen">Paul Allen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ric_Weiland" title="Ric Weiland">Ric Weiland</a>, and Gates's best friend and first business partner Kent Evans, after it caught them exploiting bugs in the operating system to obtain free computer time.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManes199434_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManes199434-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-leibovich20001231_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leibovich20001231-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The four students formed the Lakeside Programmers Club to make money.<sup id="cite_ref-leibovich20001231_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leibovich20001231-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> At the end of the ban, they offered to find bugs in CCC's software in exchange for extra computer time. Rather than use the system remotely via <a href="/wiki/Teleprinter" title="Teleprinter">Teletype</a>, Gates went to CCC's offices and studied <a href="/wiki/Source_code" title="Source code">source code</a> for various programs that ran on the system, including <a href="/wiki/Fortran" title="Fortran">Fortran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisp_(programming_language)" title="Lisp (programming language)">Lisp</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Machine_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Machine language">machine language</a>. The arrangement with CCC continued until 1970 when the company went out of business.
</p><p>The following year, a Lakeside teacher enlisted Gates and Evans to automate the school's class-scheduling system, providing them computer time and royalties in return. The duo worked diligently in order to have the program ready for their senior year. Towards the end of their junior year, Evans was killed in a mountain climbing accident, which Gates has described as one of the saddest days of his life. Gates then turned to Allen who helped him finish the system for Lakeside.<sup id="cite_ref-leibovich20001231_25-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leibovich20001231-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At 17, Gates formed a venture with Allen called <a href="/wiki/Traf-O-Data" title="Traf-O-Data">Traf-O-Data</a> to make traffic counters based on the <a href="/wiki/Intel_8008" title="Intel 8008">Intel 8008</a> processor.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGates199614_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGates199614-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> In 1972, he served as a congressional page in the House of Representatives.<sup id="cite_ref-Schuman2008_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schuman2008-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sims2018_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sims2018-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> He was a <a href="/wiki/National_Merit_Scholarship_Program" title="National Merit Scholarship Program">National Merit Scholar</a> when he graduated from Lakeside School in 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> He scored 1590 out of 1600 on the <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">Scholastic Aptitude Tests</a> (SAT) and enrolled at <a href="/wiki/Harvard_College" title="Harvard College">Harvard College</a> in the autumn of 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGates199615_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGates199615-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> He chose a pre-law major but took mathematics and graduate level computer science courses.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> While at Harvard, he met fellow student <a href="/wiki/Steve_Ballmer" title="Steve Ballmer">Steve Ballmer</a>. Gates left Harvard after two years while Ballmer stayed and graduated <i><a href="/wiki/Magna_cum_laude" class="mw-redirect" title="Magna cum laude">magna cum laude</a></i>. Years later, Ballmer succeeded Gates as Microsoft's CEO and maintained that position from 2000 until his resignation in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gates devised an algorithm for <a href="/wiki/Pancake_sorting" title="Pancake sorting">pancake sorting</a> as a solution to one of a series of unsolved problems<sup id="cite_ref-Kestenbaum2008_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kestenbaum2008-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> presented in a <a href="/wiki/Combinatorics" title="Combinatorics">combinatorics</a> class by professor <a href="/wiki/Harry_R._Lewis" title="Harry R. Lewis">Harry Lewis</a>. His solution held the record as the fastest version for over 30 years, and its successor is faster by only 2%.<sup id="cite_ref-Kestenbaum2008_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kestenbaum2008-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> His solution was formalized and published in collaboration with Harvard computer scientist <a href="/wiki/Christos_Papadimitriou" title="Christos Papadimitriou">Christos Papadimitriou</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gatespapadimitriou_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gatespapadimitriou-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gates remained in contact with Paul Allen and joined him at <a href="/wiki/Honeywell" title="Honeywell">Honeywell</a> during the summer of 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWallace199359_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWallace199359-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> In 1975, the <a href="/wiki/MITS_Altair_8800" class="mw-redirect" title="MITS Altair 8800">MITS Altair 8800</a> was released based on the <a href="/wiki/Intel_8080_CPU" class="mw-redirect" title="Intel 8080 CPU">Intel 8080 CPU</a>, and Gates and Allen saw the opportunity to start their own computer software company.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGates199618_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGates199618-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Gates dropped out of Harvard that same year. His parents were supportive of him after seeing how much he wanted to start his own company.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGates199619_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGates199619-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> He explained his decision to leave Harvard: "if things hadn't worked out, I could always go back to school. I was officially on leave."<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Microsoft">Microsoft</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Microsoft" title="History of Microsoft">History of Microsoft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft#History" title="Microsoft">Microsoft §&#160;History</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="BASIC">BASIC</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Altair_8800_Computer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Altair_8800_Computer.jpg/220px-Altair_8800_Computer.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Altair_8800_Computer.jpg/330px-Altair_8800_Computer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Altair_8800_Computer.jpg/440px-Altair_8800_Computer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1495" data-file-height="1349" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Altair_8800_Computer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>MITS <a href="/wiki/Altair_8800" title="Altair 8800">Altair 8800</a> Computer with 8-inch (200&#160;mm) floppy disk system, of which the first programming language for the machine was Microsoft's founding product, the <a href="/wiki/Altair_BASIC" title="Altair BASIC">Altair BASIC</a></div></div></div>
<p>Gates read the January 1975 issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Popular_Electronics" title="Popular Electronics">Popular Electronics</a></i> which demonstrated the <a href="/wiki/Altair_8800" title="Altair 8800">Altair 8800</a>, and he contacted <a href="/wiki/Micro_Instrumentation_and_Telemetry_Systems" title="Micro Instrumentation and Telemetry Systems">Micro Instrumentation and Telemetry Systems</a> (MITS) to inform them that he and others were working on a <a href="/wiki/BASIC" title="BASIC">BASIC</a> interpreter for the platform.<sup id="cite_ref-keyevents_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-keyevents-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> In reality, Gates and Allen did not have an Altair and had not written code for it; they merely wanted to gauge MITS's interest. MITS president <a href="/wiki/Ed_Roberts_(computers)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ed Roberts (computers)">Ed Roberts</a> agreed to meet them for a demonstration, and over the course of a few weeks they developed an Altair <a href="/wiki/Emulator" title="Emulator">emulator</a> that ran on a minicomputer, and then the BASIC interpreter. The demonstration was held at MITS's offices in <a href="/wiki/Albuquerque,_New_Mexico" title="Albuquerque, New Mexico">Albuquerque, New Mexico</a>; it was a success and resulted in a deal with MITS to distribute the interpreter as <a href="/wiki/Altair_BASIC" title="Altair BASIC">Altair BASIC</a>. MITS hired Allen,<sup id="cite_ref-thocp1_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thocp1-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> and Gates took a leave of absence from Harvard to work with him at MITS in November 1975. Allen named their partnership "Micro-Soft", a combination of "microcomputer" and "software", and their first office was in Albuquerque. The first employee Gates and Allen hired was their high school collaborator <a href="/wiki/Ric_Weiland" title="Ric Weiland">Ric Weiland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thocp1_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thocp1-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> They dropped the hyphen within a year and officially registered the trade name "Microsoft" with the Secretary of the State of New Mexico on November 26, 1976.<sup id="cite_ref-thocp1_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thocp1-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Gates never returned to Harvard to complete his studies.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>'s Altair BASIC was popular with computer hobbyists, but Gates discovered that a pre-market copy had leaked out and was being widely copied and distributed. In February 1976, he wrote an <a href="/wiki/Open_Letter_to_Hobbyists" title="Open Letter to Hobbyists">Open Letter to Hobbyists</a> in the MITS newsletter in which he asserted that more than 90% of the users of Microsoft Altair BASIC had not paid Microsoft for it and the Altair "hobby market" was in danger of eliminating the incentive for any professional developers to produce, distribute, and maintain high-quality software.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManes199481_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManes199481-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> This letter was unpopular with many computer hobbyists, but Gates persisted in his belief that software developers should be able to demand payment. Microsoft became independent of MITS in late 1976, and it continued to develop programming language software for various systems.<sup id="cite_ref-thocp1_55-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thocp1-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The company moved from Albuquerque to <a href="/wiki/Bellevue,_Washington" title="Bellevue, Washington">Bellevue, Washington</a> on January 1, 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-keyevents_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-keyevents-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gates said he personally reviewed and often rewrote every line of code that the company produced in its first five years. As the company grew he transitioned into a manager role, then an executive.<sup id="cite_ref-waterloo_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waterloo-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="IBM_partnership">IBM partnership</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, the leading supplier of computer equipment to commercial enterprises at the time, approached Microsoft in July 1980 concerning software for its upcoming personal computer, the <a href="/wiki/IBM_PC" class="mw-redirect" title="IBM PC">IBM PC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bunnell1982febmar_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bunnell1982febmar-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> IBM first proposed that Microsoft write the BASIC interpreter. IBM's representatives also mentioned that they needed an operating system, and Gates referred them to <a href="/wiki/Digital_Research" title="Digital Research">Digital Research</a> (DRI), makers of the widely used <a href="/wiki/CP/M" title="CP/M">CP/M</a> operating system.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> IBM's discussions with Digital Research went poorly, however, and they did not reach a licensing agreement. IBM representative Jack Sams mentioned the licensing difficulties during a subsequent meeting with Gates and asked if Microsoft could provide an operating system. A few weeks later, Gates and Allen proposed using <a href="/wiki/86-DOS" title="86-DOS">86-DOS</a>, an operating system similar to CP/M, that <a href="/wiki/Tim_Paterson" title="Tim Paterson">Tim Paterson</a> of <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Computer_Products" title="Seattle Computer Products">Seattle Computer Products</a> (SCP) had made for hardware similar to the PC.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Microsoft made a deal with SCP to be the exclusive licensing agent of 86-DOS, and later the full owner. Microsoft employed Paterson to adapt the operating system for the PC<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> and delivered it to IBM as <a href="/wiki/PC_DOS" class="mw-redirect" title="PC DOS">PC DOS</a> for a one-time fee of $50,000.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGates199654_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGates199654-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The contract itself only earned Microsoft a relatively small fee.  It was the prestige brought to Microsoft by IBM's adoption of their operating system that would be the origin of Microsoft's transformation from a small business to the leading software company in the world. Gates had not offered to transfer the copyright on the operating system to IBM because he believed that other personal computer makers would clone IBM's PC hardware.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGates199654_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGates199654-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> They did, making the IBM-compatible PC, running DOS, a de facto standard. The sales of <a href="/wiki/MS-DOS" title="MS-DOS">MS-DOS</a> (the version of DOS sold to customers other than IBM) made Microsoft a major player in the industry.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEManes1994193_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEManes1994193-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The press quickly identified Microsoft as being very influential on the IBM PC. <i>PC Magazine</i> asked if Gates was "the man behind the machine?".<sup id="cite_ref-bunnell1982febmar_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bunnell1982febmar-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gates oversaw Microsoft's company restructuring on June 25, 1981, which re-incorporated the company in Washington state and made Gates the president and chairman of the board, with Paul Allen as vice president and vice chairman. In early 1983, Allen left the company after receiving a <a href="/wiki/Hodgkin_lymphoma" title="Hodgkin lymphoma">Hodgkin lymphoma</a> diagnosis, effectively ending the formal business partnership between Gates and Allen, which had been strained months prior due to a contentious dispute over Microsoft equity.<sup id="cite_ref-keyevents_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-keyevents-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-before_microsoft_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-before_microsoft-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Later in the decade, Gates repaired his relationship with Allen and together the two donated millions to their childhood school Lakeside.<sup id="cite_ref-leibovich20001231_25-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leibovich20001231-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> They remained friends until Allen's death in October 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-Gates_Mourns_Allen_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gates_Mourns_Allen-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Windows">Windows</span></h3>
<p>Microsoft launched its first retail version of <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> on November 20, 1985. In August of the following year, the company struck a deal with <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> to develop a separate operating system called <a href="/wiki/OS/2" title="OS/2">OS/2</a>. Although the two companies successfully developed the first version of the new system, the partnership deteriorated due to mounting creative differences.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Management_style">Management style</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:189px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Gates_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Bill_Gates_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008.jpg/187px-Bill_Gates_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="187" height="280" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Bill_Gates_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008.jpg/280px-Bill_Gates_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Bill_Gates_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008.jpg/373px-Bill_Gates_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2731" data-file-height="4096" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Gates_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gates delivers a speech at the World Economic Forum in Switzerland, January 2008</div></div></div>
<p>Gates had primary responsibility for Microsoft's product strategy from the company's founding in 1975 until 2006. He gained a reputation for being distant from others; an industry executive complained in 1981 that "Gates is notorious for not being reachable by phone and for not returning phone calls."<sup id="cite_ref-freiberger19810831_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freiberger19810831-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> An Atari executive recalled that he showed Gates a game and defeated him 35 of 37 times. When they met again a month later, Gates "won or tied every game. He had studied the game until he solved it. That is a competitor".<sup id="cite_ref-Atari_Thorlin_Interview_2000_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Atari_Thorlin_Interview_2000-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gates met regularly with Microsoft's senior managers and program managers, and the managers described him as being verbally combative. He also berated them for perceived holes in their business strategies or proposals that placed the company's long-term interests at risk.<sup id="cite_ref-rensin_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rensin-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> He interrupted presentations with such comments as "that's the stupidest thing I've ever heard"<sup id="cite_ref-time_GOS_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time_GOS-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> and "why don't you just give up your <a href="/wiki/Employee_stock_option" title="Employee stock option">options</a> and join the <a href="/wiki/Peace_Corps" title="Peace Corps">Peace Corps</a>?"<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The target of his outburst would then have to defend the proposal in detail until Gates was fully convinced.<sup id="cite_ref-time_GOS_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time_GOS-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> When subordinates appeared to be procrastinating, he was known to remark sarcastically, "I'll do it over the weekend."<sup id="cite_ref-chapman_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chapman-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pdc97_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pdc97-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-herbold_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-herbold-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During Microsoft's early years, Gates was an active software developer, particularly in the company's programming language products, but his primary role in most of the company's history was as a manager and executive. He has not officially been on a development team since working on the <a href="/wiki/TRS-80_Model_100" title="TRS-80 Model 100">TRS-80 Model 100</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-allison1993_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allison1993-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> but he wrote code that shipped with the company's products as late as 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-pdc97_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pdc97-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Pournelle" title="Jerry Pournelle">Jerry Pournelle</a> wrote in 1985 when Gates announced <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Excel" title="Microsoft Excel">Microsoft Excel</a>: "Bill Gates likes the program, not because it's going to make him a lot of money (although I'm sure it will do that), but because it's a neat <a href="/wiki/Hack_(programmer_subculture)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hack (programmer subculture)">hack</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-pournelle198509_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pournelle198509-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 15, 2006, Gates announced that he would transition out of his role at Microsoft to dedicate more time to philanthropy. He divided his responsibilities between two successors when he placed <a href="/wiki/Ray_Ozzie" title="Ray Ozzie">Ray Ozzie</a> in charge of management and <a href="/wiki/Craig_Mundie" title="Craig Mundie">Craig Mundie</a> in charge of long-term product strategy.<sup id="cite_ref-mscorpnews_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mscorpnews-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antitrust_litigation">Antitrust litigation</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/United_States_Microsoft_antitrust_case" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Microsoft antitrust case">United States Microsoft antitrust case</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Microsoft_competition_case" class="mw-redirect" title="European Union Microsoft competition case">European Union Microsoft competition case</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_v._Microsoft_Bill_Gates_Color.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/US_v._Microsoft_Bill_Gates_Color.png/220px-US_v._Microsoft_Bill_Gates_Color.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/US_v._Microsoft_Bill_Gates_Color.png/330px-US_v._Microsoft_Bill_Gates_Color.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/US_v._Microsoft_Bill_Gates_Color.png/440px-US_v._Microsoft_Bill_Gates_Color.png 2x" data-file-width="699" data-file-height="478" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_v._Microsoft_Bill_Gates_Color.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gates giving his deposition at Microsoft on August 27, 1998</div></div></div>
<p>Gates approved of many decisions that led to <a href="/wiki/United_States_antitrust_law" title="United States antitrust law">antitrust</a> litigation over Microsoft's business practices. In the 1998 <i><a href="/wiki/United_States_v._Microsoft" class="mw-redirect" title="United States v. Microsoft">United States v. Microsoft</a></i> case, Gates gave <a href="/wiki/Deposition_(law)" title="Deposition (law)">deposition</a> testimony that several journalists characterized as evasive. He argued with examiner <a href="/wiki/David_Boies" title="David Boies">David Boies</a> over the contextual meaning of words such as "compete", "concerned", and "we". Later in the year, when portions of the videotaped deposition were played back in court, the judge was seen laughing and shaking his head.<sup id="cite_ref-GatesDepositionJudgeLaugh_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GatesDepositionJudgeLaugh-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> <i>BusinessWeek</i> reported:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Early rounds of his deposition show him offering obfuscatory answers and saying "I don't recall" so many times that even the presiding judge had to chuckle. Worse, many of the technology chief's denials and pleas of ignorance were directly refuted by prosecutors with snippets of e-mail that Gates both sent and received.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Gates later said that he had simply resisted attempts by Boies to mischaracterize his words and actions. "Did I fence with Boies? … I plead guilty… rudeness to Boies in the first degree."<sup id="cite_ref-truth_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-truth-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Despite Gates's denials, the judge ruled that Microsoft had committed <a href="/wiki/Monopolization" title="Monopolization">monopolization</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tying_(commerce)" title="Tying (commerce)">tying</a> and blocking competition, each in violation of the <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Antitrust_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Sherman Antitrust Act">Sherman Antitrust Act</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-truth_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-truth-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Microsoft">Post-Microsoft</span></h2>
<p>Since leaving day-to-day operations at Microsoft, Gates has continued his philanthropy and works on other projects.
</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_Billionaires_Index" title="Bloomberg Billionaires Index">Bloomberg Billionaires Index</a>, Gates was the world's highest-earning billionaire in 2013, as his net worth increased by US$15.8&#160;billion to US$78.5&#160;billion. As of January&#160;2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bill_Gates&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, most of Gates's assets are held in <a href="/wiki/Cascade_Investment" title="Cascade Investment">Cascade Investment</a> LLC, an entity through which he owns stakes in numerous businesses, including <a href="/wiki/Four_Seasons_Hotels_and_Resorts" title="Four Seasons Hotels and Resorts">Four Seasons Hotels and Resorts</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Corbis_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Corbis Corporation">Corbis Corp.</a><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> On February 4, 2014, Gates stepped down as chairman of Microsoft to become "technology advisor" alongside CEO <a href="/wiki/Satya_Nadella" title="Satya Nadella">Satya Nadella</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gates provided his perspective on a range of issues in a substantial interview that was published in the March 27, 2014 issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine. In the interview, Gates provided his perspective on climate change, his charitable activities, various tech companies and people involved in them, and the state of America. In response to a question about his greatest fear when he looks 50 years into the future, Gates stated: "...<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>there'll be some really bad things that'll happen in the next 50 or 100 years, but hopefully none of them on the scale of, say, a million people that you didn't expect to die from a <a href="/wiki/Pandemic" title="Pandemic">pandemic</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear</a> or <a href="/wiki/Bioterrorism" title="Bioterrorism">bioterrorism</a>." Gates also identified innovation as the "real driver of progress" and pronounced that "America's way better today than it's ever been."<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gates has expressed concern about the potential harms of <a href="/wiki/Superintelligence" title="Superintelligence">superintelligence</a>; in a <a href="/wiki/Reddit" title="Reddit">Reddit</a> "ask me anything", he stated that:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>First the machines will do a lot of jobs for us and not be super intelligent. That should be positive if we manage it well. A few decades after that though the intelligence is strong enough to be a concern. I agree with <a href="/wiki/Elon_Musk" title="Elon Musk">Elon Musk</a> and some others on this and don't understand why some people are not concerned.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>In an interview that was held at the <a href="/wiki/TED_(conference)" title="TED (conference)">TED conference</a> in March 2015, with <a href="/wiki/Baidu" title="Baidu">Baidu</a>'s CEO, <a href="/wiki/Robin_Li" title="Robin Li">Robin Li</a>, Gates said he would "highly recommend" <a href="/wiki/Nick_Bostrom" title="Nick Bostrom">Nick Bostrom</a>'s recent work, <i><a href="/wiki/Superintelligence:_Paths,_Dangers,_Strategies" title="Superintelligence: Paths, Dangers, Strategies">Superintelligence: Paths, Dangers, Strategies</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> During the conference, Gates warned that the world was not prepared for the next pandemic, a situation that would come to pass in late 2019 when the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> began.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> In March 2018, Gates met at his home in Seattle with <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_bin_Salman" title="Mohammed bin Salman">Mohammed bin Salman</a>, the reformist crown prince and de facto ruler of <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> to discuss investment opportunities for <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Vision_2030" title="Saudi Vision 2030">Saudi Vision 2030</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> In June 2019, Gates admitted that losing the <a href="/wiki/Mobile_operating_system" title="Mobile operating system">mobile operating system</a> race to <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> was his biggest mistake. He stated that it was within their <a href="/wiki/Skill_set" class="mw-redirect" title="Skill set">skill set</a> of being the dominant player, but partially blames the <a href="/wiki/Antitrust_case" class="mw-redirect" title="Antitrust case">antitrust</a> litigation during the time.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> That same year, Gates became an Advisory Board Member of the <a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_L.P.#Bloomberg_New_Economy_Forum" title="Bloomberg L.P.">Bloomberg New Economy Forum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 13, 2020, Microsoft announced Gates would be leaving his board positions at Berkshire Hathaway and Microsoft to dedicate his efforts in philanthropic endeavors such as climate change, global health and development, and education.<sup id="cite_ref-Haselton_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haselton-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bill_and_Melinda_Gates_Foundation">Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bill_%26_Melinda_Gates_Foundation" title="Bill &amp; Melinda Gates Foundation">Bill &amp; Melinda Gates Foundation</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Millennium_Development_Goals_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Millennium_Development_Goals_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008.jpg/220px-Millennium_Development_Goals_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Millennium_Development_Goals_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008.jpg/330px-Millennium_Development_Goals_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Millennium_Development_Goals_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008.jpg/440px-Millennium_Development_Goals_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2705" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Millennium_Development_Goals_-_World_Economic_Forum_Annual_Meeting_Davos_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gates with <a href="/wiki/Bono" title="Bono">Bono</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen_Rania_of_Jordan" title="Queen Rania of Jordan">Queen Rania of Jordan</a>, former British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Brown" title="Gordon Brown">Gordon Brown</a>, President <a href="/wiki/Umaru_Musa_Yar%27Adua" title="Umaru Musa Yar&#39;Adua">Umaru Yar'Adua</a> of Nigeria and others during the Annual Meeting 2008 of the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a></div></div></div>
<p>Gates studied the work of <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie" title="Andrew Carnegie">Andrew Carnegie</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller" title="John D. Rockefeller">John D. Rockefeller</a>, and donated some of his Microsoft stock in 1994 to create the "William H. Gates Foundation." In 2000, Gates and his wife combined three family foundations and Gates donated stock valued at $5&#160;billion to create the charitable <a href="/wiki/Bill_%26_Melinda_Gates_Foundation" title="Bill &amp; Melinda Gates Foundation">Bill &amp; Melinda Gates Foundation</a>, which was identified by the Funds for NGOs company in 2013, as the world's wealthiest charitable foundation, with assets reportedly valued at more than $34.6&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The foundation allows benefactors to access information that shows how its money is being spent, unlike other major charitable organizations such as the <a href="/wiki/Wellcome_Trust" title="Wellcome Trust">Wellcome Trust</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Gates, through his foundation, also donated $20&#160;million to <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_University" title="Carnegie Mellon University">Carnegie Mellon University</a> for a new building to be named Gates Center for Computer Science which opened in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gates has credited the generosity and extensive philanthropy of <a href="/wiki/David_Rockefeller" title="David Rockefeller">David Rockefeller</a> as a major influence. Gates and his father met with Rockefeller several times, and their charity work is partly modeled on the <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_family" title="Rockefeller family">Rockefeller family</a>'s philanthropic focus, whereby they are interested in tackling the global problems that are ignored by governments and other organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-bill_foundation_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bill_foundation-101">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bill_Gates&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Bill and Melinda Gates were the second-most generous philanthropists in America, having given over $28&#160;billion to charity;<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> the couple plan to eventually donate 95% of their wealth to charity.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The foundation is organized into five program areas: Global Development Division, Global Health Division, United States Division, and Global Policy &amp; Advocacy Division. Among others, it supports a wide range of public health projects, granting aid to fight transmissible diseases such <a href="/wiki/AIDS" class="mw-redirect" title="AIDS">AIDS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, as well as widespread vaccine programs to eradicate <a href="/wiki/Polio" title="Polio">polio</a>. It grants funds to learning institutes and libraries and supports scholarships at universities. The foundation established a water, sanitation and hygiene program to provide sustainable sanitation services in poor countries.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Its agriculture division  supports the <a href="/wiki/International_Rice_Research_Institute" title="International Rice Research Institute">International Rice Research Institute</a> in developing <a href="/wiki/Golden_Rice" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Rice">Golden Rice</a>, a genetically modified rice variant used to combat <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_A_deficiency" title="Vitamin A deficiency">vitamin A deficiency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The goal of the foundation is to provide 120&#160;million women and girls, in the poorest countries, with high-quality contraceptive information and services, with the longer-term goal of universal access to voluntary <a href="/wiki/Family_planning" title="Family planning">family planning</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> criticized the foundation for investing its assets in companies that have been accused of worsening poverty, pollution and pharmaceutical firms that do not sell to <a href="/wiki/Developing_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing countries">developing countries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Although the foundation announced a review of its investments to assess social responsibility,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> it was subsequently canceled and upheld its policy of investing for maximum return, while using voting rights to influence company practices.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Gates_at_Singapore_FinTech_Festival_2020.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Bill_Gates_at_Singapore_FinTech_Festival_2020.jpg/220px-Bill_Gates_at_Singapore_FinTech_Festival_2020.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Bill_Gates_at_Singapore_FinTech_Festival_2020.jpg/330px-Bill_Gates_at_Singapore_FinTech_Festival_2020.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Bill_Gates_at_Singapore_FinTech_Festival_2020.jpg/440px-Bill_Gates_at_Singapore_FinTech_Festival_2020.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1152" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bill_Gates_at_Singapore_FinTech_Festival_2020.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gates in a fireside chat moderated by <a href="/wiki/Shereen_Bhan" title="Shereen Bhan">Shereen Bhan</a> virtually at the <a href="/wiki/Singapore_FinTech_Festival" title="Singapore FinTech Festival">Singapore FinTech Festival</a> 2020.</div></div></div>
<p>Gates delivered his thoughts in a fireside chat moderated by journalist and news anchor <a href="/wiki/Shereen_Bhan" title="Shereen Bhan">Shereen Bhan</a> virtually at the <a href="/wiki/Singapore_FinTech_Festival" title="Singapore FinTech Festival">Singapore FinTech Festival</a> on December 8, 2020 on the topic, <i>“Building Infrastructure for Resilience: What the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19</a> Response Can Teach Us About How to Scale Financial Inclusion”</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-billgates_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billgates-110">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Governments are there to think ahead to bad things that might happen. In the case of (the Covid-19) pandemic, not enough was done. We can't forget that another pandemic will come and we'll need to invest in being ready in that, ......while not forgetting that we were not prepared and we're going to have to invest - just like having a fire department - some money in an intelligent way and actually simulate what might happen and make sure that we're ready for it.<sup id="cite_ref-billgates_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billgates-110">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_donations">Personal donations</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Melinda_Gates" title="Melinda Gates">Melinda Gates</a> suggested that people should emulate the philanthropic efforts of the Salwen family, who sold their home and gave away half of its value, as detailed in their book, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Power_of_Half" title="The Power of Half">The Power of Half</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Gates and his wife invited Joan Salwen to Seattle to speak about what the family had done, and on December 9, 2010, Bill and Melinda Gates and investor <a href="/wiki/Warren_Buffett" title="Warren Buffett">Warren Buffett</a> each signed a commitment they called the "<a href="/wiki/Giving_Pledge" class="mw-redirect" title="Giving Pledge">Giving Pledge</a>", which is a commitment by all three to donate at least half of their wealth, over the course of time, to charity.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gates has also provided personal donations to educational institutions. In 1999, Gates donated $20&#160;million to the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a> for the construction of a computer laboratory named the "William H. Gates Building" that was designed by architect <a href="/wiki/Frank_Gehry" title="Frank Gehry">Frank Gehry</a>. While Microsoft had previously given financial support to the institution, this was the first personal donation received from Gates.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Maxwell Dworkin Laboratory of the <a href="/wiki/Harvard_John_A._Paulson_School_of_Engineering_and_Applied_Sciences" title="Harvard John A. Paulson School of Engineering and Applied Sciences">Harvard John A. Paulson School of Engineering and Applied Sciences</a> is named after the mothers of both Gates and Microsoft President Steven A. Ballmer, both of whom were students (Ballmer was a member of the School's graduating class of 1977, while Gates left his studies for Microsoft), and donated funds for the laboratory's construction.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Gates also donated $6&#160;million to the construction of the Gates Computer Science Building, completed in January 1996, on the campus of <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>. The building contains the Computer Science Department and the Computer Systems Laboratory (CSL) of Stanford's Engineering department.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2005, Gates and his foundation have taken an interest in solving global <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a> problems. For example, they announced the "Reinvent the Toilet Challenge", which has received considerable media interest.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-118">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> To raise awareness for the topic of sanitation and possible solutions, Gates drank water that was "produced from human feces" in 2014&#160;– it was produced from a <a href="/wiki/Sewage_sludge_treatment" title="Sewage sludge treatment">sewage sludge treatment</a> process called the <a href="/wiki/Omni_Processor" title="Omni Processor">Omni Processor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> In early 2015, he also appeared with <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Fallon" title="Jimmy Fallon">Jimmy Fallon</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show" title="The Tonight Show">The Tonight Show</a></i> and challenged him to see if he could taste the difference between this <a href="/wiki/Reclaimed_water" title="Reclaimed water">reclaimed water</a> or bottled water.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2017, Gates said he would give $50&#160;million to the Dementia Discovery Fund, a venture capital fund that seeks treatment for <a href="/wiki/Alzheimer%27s_disease" title="Alzheimer&#39;s disease">Alzheimer's disease</a>. He also pledged an additional $50&#160;million to start-up ventures working in Alzheimer's research.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Bill and Melinda Gates have said that they intend to leave their three children $10&#160;million each as their inheritance. With only $30&#160;million kept in the family, they are expected to give away about 99.96% of their wealth.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> On August 25, 2018, Gates distributed $600,000 through his foundation via UNICEF which is helping flood affected victims in <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">Kerala</a>, India.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Charity_sports_events">Charity sports events</span></h3>
<p>On April 29, 2017, Gates partnered with Swiss tennis legend <a href="/wiki/Roger_Federer" title="Roger Federer">Roger Federer</a> in play in the <a href="/wiki/Match_for_Africa#Match_for_Africa_4" title="Match for Africa">Match for Africa 4</a>, a noncompetitive tennis match at a sold-out <a href="/wiki/Key_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Key Arena">Key Arena</a> in Seattle. The event was in support of <a href="/wiki/Roger_Federer_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Roger Federer Foundation">Roger Federer Foundation</a>'s charity efforts in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Federer and Gates played against <a href="/wiki/John_Isner" title="John Isner">John Isner</a>, the top-ranked American player for much of this decade, and <a href="/wiki/Mike_McCready" title="Mike McCready">Mike McCready</a>, the lead guitarist for <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Jam" title="Pearl Jam">Pearl Jam</a>. The pair won the match 6 to 4. Overall, they raised $2&#160;million for children in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-match4_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-match4-126">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> The following year, Gates and Federer returned to play in the <a href="/wiki/Match_for_Africa#Match_for_Africa_5" title="Match for Africa">Match for Africa 5</a> on March 5, 2018, at San Jose's <a href="/wiki/SAP_Center" title="SAP Center">SAP Center</a>. Their opponents were <a href="/wiki/Jack_Sock" title="Jack Sock">Jack Sock</a>, one of the top American players and a grand slam winner in doubles, and <a href="/wiki/Savannah_Guthrie" title="Savannah Guthrie">Savannah Guthrie</a>, a co-anchor for <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Today_(U.S._TV_program)" class="mw-redirect" title="Today (U.S. TV program)">Today</a></i> show. Gates and Federer recorded their second match victory together by a score of 6–3 and the event raised over $2.5&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-match5_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-match5-127">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Work_on_energy_and_climate_change">Work on energy and climate change</span></h2><p>
Gates considers <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> and <a href="/wiki/Energy_access" class="mw-redirect" title="Energy access">global access to energy</a> to be critical, interrelated issues. He has urged governments and the private sector to invest in research and development to make clean, reliable energy cheaper. Gates envisions that a breakthrough innovation in <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_energy" title="Sustainable energy">sustainable energy</a> technology could drive down both greenhouse gas emissions and poverty, and bring economic benefits by stabilizing energy prices.<sup id="cite_ref-:22_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:22-128">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, he said:</p><blockquote class="quote-frame pullquote toccolours" style="float:none; display:table; border: 1px solid #aaa;"><div style="padding: 10px 15px 10px 15px;">If you gave me the choice between picking the next 10 presidents or ensuring that energy is environmentally friendly and a quarter as costly, I'd pick the energy thing.<sup id="cite_ref-WIRED_2011_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WIRED_2011-129">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</div></blockquote><p> In 2015, he wrote about the challenge of transitioning the world's energy system from one based primarily on fossil fuels to one based on sustainable energy sources. Global <a href="/wiki/Energy_transitions" class="mw-redirect" title="Energy transitions">energy transitions</a> have historically taken decades. He wrote, “I believe we can make this transition faster, both because the pace of innovation is accelerating, and because we have never had such an urgent reason to move from one source of energy to another.”<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> This rapid transition, according to Gates, would depend on increased government funding for basic research and financially risky private-sector investment, to enable innovation in diverse areas such as <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear energy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grid_energy_storage" title="Grid energy storage">grid energy storage</a> to facilitate greater use of solar and wind energy, and <a href="/wiki/Solar_fuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar fuels">solar fuels</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-131">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gates spearheaded two initiatives that he announced at the <a href="/wiki/2015_United_Nations_Climate_Change_Conference" title="2015 United Nations Climate Change Conference">2015 United Nations Climate Change Conference</a> in Paris. One was <a href="/wiki/Mission_Innovation" title="Mission Innovation">Mission Innovation</a>, in which 20 national governments pledged to double their spending on research and development for carbon-free energy over five years.<sup id="cite_ref-:22_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:22-128">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Another initiative was <a href="/wiki/Breakthrough_Energy" title="Breakthrough Energy">Breakthrough Energy</a>, a group of investors who agreed to fund high-risk startups in clean energy technologies. Gates, who had already invested $1 billion of his own money in innovative energy startups, committed a further $1 billion to Breakthrough Energy.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-131">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> In December 2020, he called for the U.S. federal government to create institutes for clean energy research, analogous to the <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">National Institutes of Health</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>
Gates's views have been criticized as undermining strategies to aggressively deploy existing solar and wind energy technologies, which have also led to innovation and to plummeting costs.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> He has also been criticised for holding a large stake in  <a href="/wiki/Signature_Aviation" title="Signature Aviation">Signature Aviation</a>, a company that services emissions-intensive private jets.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>  In 2019, he began to <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel_divestment" title="Fossil fuel divestment">divest from fossil fuels</a>. He does not expect divestment itself to have much practical impact, but says that if his efforts to provide alternatives were to fail, he would not want to personally benefit from an increase in fossil fuel stock prices.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>  </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div id="mwe_player_0" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:220px;" videopayload="&lt;div class=&quot;mediaContainer&quot;
